   <script language="JavaScript" type="text/javascript">
    <!-- to hide script contents from old browsers
 
 
 	/*
 	 *	This script was adapted from C sources written by
 	 *	Scott E. Lee, which contain the following copyright notice:
 	 *
 	 *	Copyright 1993-1995, Scott E. Lee, all rights reserved.
 	 *	Permission granted to use, copy, modify, distribute and sell so long as
 	 *	the above copyright and this permission statement are retained in all

 	var GREG_SDN_OFFSET = 32045,
 		DAYS_PER_5_MONTHS = 153,
 		DAYS_PER_4_YEARS = 1461,
 		DAYS_PER_400_YEARS = 146097;
 	var HALAKIM_PER_HOUR = 1080,
 		HALAKIM_PER_DAY = 25920,
 		HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE = ((29 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY) + 13753),
 		HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE = (HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * (12 * 19 + 7));
 	var HEB_SDN_OFFSET = 347997,
 		NEW_MOON_OF_CREATION = 31524,
 		NOON = (18 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR),
 		AM3_11_20 = ((9 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR) + 204),
 		AM9_32_43 = ((15 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR) + 589);
 	var SUN = 0,
 		MON = 1,
 		TUES = 2,
 		WED = 3,
 		THUR = 4,
 		FRI = 5,
 		SAT = 6;
 	var today = null,
 		afterSundown = false,
 		hebrewMonth = 0,
 		hebrewDate = 0,
 		hebrewYear = 0,
 		metonicCycle = 0,
 		metonicYear = 0,
 		moladDay = 0,
 		moladHalakim = 0;
 	var gWeekday = new weekdayarr("Sun","Mon","Tues","Wednes","Thurs","Fri","Satur");
 	var gMonth = new gregmontharr("January","February","March","April","May","June","July","August","September","October","November","December");
 	var hMonth = new hebrewmontharr("Tishrei","Heshvan","Kislev","Tevet","Shevat","AdarI","AdarII","Nisan","Iyyar","Sivan","Tammuz","Av","Elul");
 	var mpy = new monthsperyeararr(12,12,13,12,12,13,12,13,12,12,13,12,12,13,12,12,13,12,13);
 
 	function weekdayarr(d0,d1,d2,d3,d4,d5,d6)
 	{
 		this[0] = d0; this[1] = d1; this[2] = d2; this[3] = d3;
 		this[4] = d4; this[5] = d5; this[6] = d6;
 	}
 
 	function gregmontharr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,m10,m11)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 	}
 
 	function hebrewmontharr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,m10,m11,m12,m13)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 		this[12] = m12; this[13] = m13;
 	}
 
 	function monthsperyeararr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,
 							  m10,m11,m12,m13,m14,m15,m16,m17,m18)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 		this[12] = m8; this[13] = m13; this[14] = m14; this[15] = m15;
 		this[16] = m16; this[17] = m17; this[18] = m18;
 	}
 	function getToday()
 	{
 		if(today == null) {
 			today = new Date();
 
 			afterSundown = (today.getHours() >= 19);
 		}
 	}
 	function displayWeekday()
 	{
 		document.writeln(gWeekday[today.getDay()] + "day");
 	}
 	function getFullYear(d)
 	{
 	    var y = d.getYear();
 
 	    if (y < 1000)
 	    	y += 1900;
 
 	    return y;
 	}
 
 	function displayGregorianDate()
 	{
 		document.writeln(gMonth[today.getMonth()] + " " + today.getDate() + ", " + getFullYear(today));
 	}
 	function displayHebrewDate()
 	{
 		if(hebrewDate != 0 && hebrewMonth != 0 && hebrewYear != 0)
 			document.writeln(hebrewDate + " " + hMonth[hebrewMonth-1] + " " + hebrewYear);
 	}
 	function GregorianToSdn(inputYear,inputMonth,inputDay)
 	{
 		var year = 0,
 			month = 0,
 			sdn;
 		// Make year a positive number
 		if (inputYear < 0)
 			year = inputYear + 4801;
 		else
 			year = inputYear + 4800;
 		// Adjust the start of the year
 		if (inputMonth > 2) {
 			month = inputMonth - 3;
 		}
 		else {
 			month = inputMonth + 9;
 			year--;
 		}
 		sdn	 = Math.floor((Math.floor(year / 100) * DAYS_PER_400_YEARS) / 4);
 		sdn += Math.floor(((year % 100) * DAYS_PER_4_YEARS) / 4);
 		sdn += Math.floor((month * DAYS_PER_5_MONTHS + 2) / 5);
 		sdn += inputDay - GREG_SDN_OFFSET;
 
 		if(afterSundown) {
 			sdn++;
 		}
 		return sdn;
 	}
 	function SdnToHebrew(sdn)
 	{
 		var inputDay,
 			tishri1 = 0,
 			tishri1After = 0,
 			yearLength = 0,
 		inputDay = sdn - HEB_SDN_OFFSET;
 		FindTishriMolad(inputDay);
 		tishri1 = Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 		if (inputDay >= tishri1) {
 			// It found Tishri 1 at the start of the year.
 			hebrewYear = metonicCycle * 19 + metonicYear + 1;
 			if (inputDay < tishri1 + 59) {
 				if (inputDay < tishri1 + 30) {
 					hebrewMonth = 1;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 1;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 2;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 - 29;
 				}
 				return;
 			}
 			// We need the length of the year to figure this out,so find Tishri 1 of the next year.
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * mpy[metonicYear];
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 			tishri1After = Tishri1((metonicYear + 1) % 19,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 		}
 		else {
 			// It found Tishri 1 at the end of the year.
 			hebrewYear = metonicCycle * 19 + metonicYear;
 			if (inputDay >= tishri1 - 177) {
 				// It is one of the last 6 months of the year.
 				if (inputDay > tishri1 - 30) {
 					hebrewMonth = 13;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 30;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 60) {
 					hebrewMonth = 12;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 60;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 89) {
 					hebrewMonth = 11;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 89;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 119) {
 					hebrewMonth = 10;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 119;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 148) {
 					hebrewMonth = 9;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 148;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 8;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 178;
 				}
 				return;
 			}
 			else {
 				if (mpy[(hebrewYear - 1) % 19] == 13) {
 					hebrewMonth = 7;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 207;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 6;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 207;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 				}
 				if (hebrewDate > 0)
 					return;
 				hebrewMonth--;
 				hebrewDate += 29;
 				if (hebrewDate > 0)
 					return;
 				// We need the length of the year to figure this out,so find Tishri 1 of this year.
 				tishri1After = tishri1;
 				FindTishriMolad(moladDay - 365);
 				tishri1 = Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 			}
 		}
 		yearLength = tishri1After - tishri1;
 		moladDay = inputDay - tishri1 - 29;
 		if (yearLength == 355 || yearLength == 385) {
 			// Heshvan has 30 days
 			if (moladDay <= 30) {
 				hebrewMonth = 2;
 				hebrewDate = moladDay;
 				return;
 			}
 			moladDay -= 30;
 		}
 		else {
 			// Heshvan has 29 days
 			if (moladDay <= 29) {
 				hebrewMonth = 2;
 				hebrewDate = moladDay;
 				return;
 			}
 			moladDay -= 29;
 		}
 		// It has to be Kislev.
 		hebrewMonth = 3;
 		hebrewDate = moladDay;
 	}
 	function FindTishriMolad(inputDay)
 	{
 		// Estimate the metonic cycle number.  Note that this may be an under
 		// estimate because there are 6939.6896 days in a metonic cycle not
 		// 6940,but it will never be an over estimate.	 The loop below will
 		// correct for any error in this estimate.
 		metonicCycle = Math.floor((inputDay + 310) / 6940);
 		// Calculate the time of the starting molad for this metonic cycle.
 		MoladOfMetonicCycle();
 		// If the above was an under estimate,increment the cycle number until
 		// the correct one is found.  For modern dates this loop is about 98.6%
 		// likely to not execute,even once,because the above estimate is
 		// really quite close.
 		while (moladDay < inputDay - 6940 + 310) {
 			metonicCycle++;
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE;
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		}
 		// Find the molad of Tishri closest to this date.
 		for (metonicYear = 0; metonicYear < 18; metonicYear++) {
 			if (moladDay > inputDay - 74)
 				break;
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * mpy[metonicYear];
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		}
 	}
 	function MoladOfMetonicCycle()
 	{
 		var r1,r2,d1,d2;
 		// Start with the time of the first molad after creation.
 		r1 = NEW_MOON_OF_CREATION;
 		// Calculate gMetonicCycle * HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE.	 The upper 32
 		// bits of the result will be in r2 and the lower 16 bits will be in r1.
 		r1 += metonicCycle * (HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE & 0xFFFF);
 		r2 = r1 >> 16;
 		r2 += metonicCycle * ((HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE >> 16) & 0xFFFF);
 		// Calculate r2r1 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY.  The remainder will be in r1,the
 		// upper 16 bits of the quotient will be in d2 and the lower 16 bits
 		// will be in d1.
 		d2 = Math.floor(r2 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 		r2 -= d2 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		r1 = (r2 << 16) | (r1 & 0xFFFF);
 		d1 = Math.floor(r1 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 		r1 -= d1 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		moladDay = (d2 << 16) | d1;
 		moladHalakim = r1;
 	}
 	function Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim)
 	{
 		var tishri1 = moladDay;
 		var dow = tishri1 % 7;
 		var leapYear =	metonicYear == 2 || metonicYear == 5 || metonicYear == 7 || metonicYear == 10 ||
 						metonicYear == 13 || metonicYear == 16 || metonicYear == 18;
 		var lastWasLeapYear =	metonicYear == 3 || metonicYear == 6 || metonicYear == 8 || metonicYear == 11 ||
 								metonicYear == 14 || metonicYear == 17 || metonicYear == 0;
 		// Apply rules 2,3 and 4
 		if ((moladHalakim >= NOON) ||
 			((!leapYear) && dow == TUES && moladHalakim >= AM3_11_20) ||
 			(lastWasLeapYear && dow == MON && moladHalakim >= AM9_32_43))
 		{
 			tishri1++;
 			dow++;
 			if (dow == 7)
 				dow = 0;
 		}
 		// Apply rule 1 after the others because it can cause an additional delay of one day.
 		if (dow == WED || dow == FRI || dow == SUN) {
 			tishri1++;
 		}
 		return tishri1;
 	}
 	//	end hiding contents from old browsers  -->

 	var GREG_SDN_OFFSET = 32045,
 		DAYS_PER_5_MONTHS = 153,
 		DAYS_PER_4_YEARS = 1461,
 		DAYS_PER_400_YEARS = 146097;
 	var HALAKIM_PER_HOUR = 1080,
 		HALAKIM_PER_DAY = 25920,
 		HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE = ((29 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY) + 13753),
 		HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE = (HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * (12 * 19 + 7));
 	var HEB_SDN_OFFSET = 347997,
 		NEW_MOON_OF_CREATION = 31524,
 		NOON = (18 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR),
 		AM3_11_20 = ((9 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR) + 204),
 		AM9_32_43 = ((15 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR) + 589);

 		MON = 1,

 		WED = 3,
 		THUR = 4,
 		FRI = 5,
 		SAT = 6;

 		afterSundown = false,

 		hebrewDate = 0,

 		moladHalakim = 0;

 	function weekdayarr(d0,d1,d2,d3,d4,d5,d6)
 	{
 		this[0] = d0; this[1] = d1; this[2] = d2; this[3] = d3;
 		this[4] = d4; this[5] = d5; this[6] = d6;
 	}
 
 	function gregmontharr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,m10,m11)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 	}
 
 	function hebrewmontharr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,m10,m11,m12,m13)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 		this[12] = m12; this[13] = m13;
 	}
 
 	function monthsperyeararr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,
 							  m10,m11,m12,m13,m14,m15,m16,m17,m18)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 		this[12] = m8; this[13] = m13; this[14] = m14; this[15] = m15;
 		this[16] = m16; this[17] = m17; this[18] = m18;
 	}
 	function getToday()
 	{
 		if(today == null) {
 			today = new Date();
 
 			afterSundown = (today.getHours() >= 19);
 		}
 	}
 	function displayWeekday()
 	{
 		document.writeln(gWeekday[today.getDay()] + "day");
 	}
 	function getFullYear(d)
 	{
 	    var y = d.getYear();
 
 	    if (y < 1000)
 	    	y += 1900;
 
 	    return y;
 	}
 
 	function displayGregorianDate()
 	{
 		document.writeln(gMonth[today.getMonth()] + " " + today.getDate() + ", " + getFullYear(today));
 	}
 	function displayHebrewDate()
 	{
 		if(hebrewDate != 0 && hebrewMonth != 0 && hebrewYear != 0)
 			document.writeln(hebrewDate + " " + hMonth[hebrewMonth-1] + " " + hebrewYear);
 	}
 	function GregorianToSdn(inputYear,inputMonth,inputDay)
 	{
 		var year = 0,
 			month = 0,
 			sdn;
 		// Make year a positive number
 		if (inputYear < 0)
 			year = inputYear + 4801;
 		else
 			year = inputYear + 4800;
 		// Adjust the start of the year
 		if (inputMonth > 2) {
 			month = inputMonth - 3;
 		}
 		else {
 			month = inputMonth + 9;
 			year--;
 		}
 		sdn	 = Math.floor((Math.floor(year / 100) * DAYS_PER_400_YEARS) / 4);
 		sdn += Math.floor(((year % 100) * DAYS_PER_4_YEARS) / 4);
 		sdn += Math.floor((month * DAYS_PER_5_MONTHS + 2) / 5);
 		sdn += inputDay - GREG_SDN_OFFSET;
 
 		if(afterSundown) {
 			sdn++;
 		}
 		return sdn;
 	}
 	function SdnToHebrew(sdn)
 	{
 		var inputDay,
 			tishri1 = 0,
 			tishri1After = 0,
 			yearLength = 0,
 		inputDay = sdn - HEB_SDN_OFFSET;
 		FindTishriMolad(inputDay);
 		tishri1 = Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 		if (inputDay >= tishri1) {
 			// It found Tishri 1 at the start of the year.
 			hebrewYear = metonicCycle * 19 + metonicYear + 1;
 			if (inputDay < tishri1 + 59) {
 				if (inputDay < tishri1 + 30) {
 					hebrewMonth = 1;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 1;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 2;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 - 29;
 				}
 				return;
 			}
 			// We need the length of the year to figure this out,so find Tishri 1 of the next year.
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * mpy[metonicYear];
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 			tishri1After = Tishri1((metonicYear + 1) % 19,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 		}
 		else {
 			// It found Tishri 1 at the end of the year.
 			hebrewYear = metonicCycle * 19 + metonicYear;
 			if (inputDay >= tishri1 - 177) {
 				// It is one of the last 6 months of the year.
 				if (inputDay > tishri1 - 30) {
 					hebrewMonth = 13;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 30;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 60) {
 					hebrewMonth = 12;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 60;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 89) {
 					hebrewMonth = 11;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 89;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 119) {
 					hebrewMonth = 10;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 119;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 148) {
 					hebrewMonth = 9;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 148;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 8;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 178;
 				}
 				return;
 			}
 			else {
 				if (mpy[(hebrewYear - 1) % 19] == 13) {
 					hebrewMonth = 7;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 207;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 6;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 207;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 				}
 				if (hebrewDate > 0)
 					return;
 				hebrewMonth--;
 				hebrewDate += 29;
 				if (hebrewDate > 0)
 					return;
 				// We need the length of the year to figure this out,so find Tishri 1 of this year.
 				tishri1After = tishri1;
 				FindTishriMolad(moladDay - 365);
 				tishri1 = Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 			}
 		}
 		yearLength = tishri1After - tishri1;
 		moladDay = inputDay - tishri1 - 29;
 		if (yearLength == 355 || yearLength == 385) {
 			// Heshvan has 30 days
 			if (moladDay <= 30) {
 				hebrewMonth = 2;
 				hebrewDate = moladDay;
 				return;
 			}
 			moladDay -= 30;
 		}
 		else {
 			// Heshvan has 29 days
 			if (moladDay <= 29) {
 				hebrewMonth = 2;
 				hebrewDate = moladDay;
 				return;
 			}
 			moladDay -= 29;
 		}
 		// It has to be Kislev.
 		hebrewMonth = 3;
 		hebrewDate = moladDay;
 	}
 	function FindTishriMolad(inputDay)
 	{
 		// Estimate the metonic cycle number.  Note that this may be an under
 		// estimate because there are 6939.6896 days in a metonic cycle not
 		// 6940,but it will never be an over estimate.	 The loop below will
 		// correct for any error in this estimate.
 		metonicCycle = Math.floor((inputDay + 310) / 6940);
 		// Calculate the time of the starting molad for this metonic cycle.
 		MoladOfMetonicCycle();
 		// If the above was an under estimate,increment the cycle number until
 		// the correct one is found.  For modern dates this loop is about 98.6%
 		// likely to not execute,even once,because the above estimate is
 		// really quite close.
 		while (moladDay < inputDay - 6940 + 310) {
 			metonicCycle++;
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE;
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		}
 		// Find the molad of Tishri closest to this date.
 		for (metonicYear = 0; metonicYear < 18; metonicYear++) {
 			if (moladDay > inputDay - 74)
 				break;
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * mpy[metonicYear];
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		}
 	}
 	function MoladOfMetonicCycle()
 	{
 		var r1,r2,d1,d2;
 		// Start with the time of the first molad after creation.
 		r1 = NEW_MOON_OF_CREATION;
 		// Calculate gMetonicCycle * HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE.	 The upper 32
 		// bits of the result will be in r2 and the lower 16 bits will be in r1.
 		r1 += metonicCycle * (HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE & 0xFFFF);
 		r2 = r1 >> 16;
 		r2 += metonicCycle * ((HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE >> 16) & 0xFFFF);
 		// Calculate r2r1 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY.  The remainder will be in r1,the
 		// upper 16 bits of the quotient will be in d2 and the lower 16 bits
 		// will be in d1.
 		d2 = Math.floor(r2 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 		r2 -= d2 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		r1 = (r2 << 16) | (r1 & 0xFFFF);
 		d1 = Math.floor(r1 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 		r1 -= d1 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		moladDay = (d2 << 16) | d1;
 		moladHalakim = r1;
 	}
 	function Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim)
 	{
 		var tishri1 = moladDay;
 		var dow = tishri1 % 7;
 		var leapYear =	metonicYear == 2 || metonicYear == 5 || metonicYear == 7 || metonicYear == 10 ||
 						metonicYear == 13 || metonicYear == 16 || metonicYear == 18;
 		var lastWasLeapYear =	metonicYear == 3 || metonicYear == 6 || metonicYear == 8 || metonicYear == 11 ||
 								metonicYear == 14 || metonicYear == 17 || metonicYear == 0;
 		// Apply rules 2,3 and 4
 		if ((moladHalakim >= NOON) ||
 			((!leapYear) && dow == TUES && moladHalakim >= AM3_11_20) ||
 			(lastWasLeapYear && dow == MON && moladHalakim >= AM9_32_43))
 		{
 			tishri1++;
 			dow++;
 			if (dow == 7)
 				dow = 0;
 		}
 		// Apply rule 1 after the others because it can cause an additional delay of one day.
 		if (dow == WED || dow == FRI || dow == SUN) {
 			tishri1++;
 		}
 		return tishri1;
 	}
 	//	end hiding contents from old browsers  -->

           <script>
            <!--  Hebrew Date -->
 // (C) 2000 www.CodeLifter.com
 // http://www.codelifter.com
 // Free for all users, but leave in this  header
 function printWindow(){
    bV = parseInt(navigator.appVersion)
    if (bV >= 4) window.print()
 }
           </script>
           <script language="JavaScript" type="text/javascript">
            <!-- to hide script contents from old browsers
 
 
 	/*
 	 *	This script was adapted from C sources written by
 	 *	Scott E. Lee, which contain the following copyright notice:
 	 *
 	 *	Copyright 1993-1995, Scott E. Lee, all rights reserved.
 	 *	Permission granted to use, copy, modify, distribute and sell so long as
 	 *	the above copyright and this permission statement are retained in all
 	 *	copies.  THERE IS NO WARRANTY - USE AT YOUR OWN RISK.
 	 *
 	 *	Bill Hastings
 	 *	RBI Software Systems
 	 *	bhastings@rbi.com
 	 */
 	var GREG_SDN_OFFSET = 32045,
 		DAYS_PER_5_MONTHS = 153,
 		DAYS_PER_4_YEARS = 1461,
 		DAYS_PER_400_YEARS = 146097;
 	var HALAKIM_PER_HOUR = 1080,
 		HALAKIM_PER_DAY = 25920,
 		HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE = ((29 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY) + 13753),
 		HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE = (HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * (12 * 19 + 7));
 	var HEB_SDN_OFFSET = 347997,
 		NEW_MOON_OF_CREATION = 31524,
 		NOON = (18 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR),
 		AM3_11_20 = ((9 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR) + 204),
 		AM9_32_43 = ((15 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR) + 589);
 	var SUN = 0,
 		MON = 1,
 		TUES = 2,
 		WED = 3,
 		THUR = 4,
 		FRI = 5,
 		SAT = 6;
 	var today = null,
 		afterSundown = false,
 		hebrewMonth = 0,
 		hebrewDate = 0,
 		hebrewYear = 0,
 		metonicCycle = 0,
 		metonicYear = 0,
 		moladDay = 0,
 		moladHalakim = 0;
 	var gWeekday = new weekdayarr("Sun","Mon","Tues","Wednes","Thurs","Fri","Satur");
 	var gMonth = new gregmontharr("January","February","March","April","May","June","July","August","September","October","November","December");
 	var hMonth = new hebrewmontharr("Tishrei","Heshvan","Kislev","Tevet","Shevat","AdarI","AdarII","Nisan","Iyyar","Sivan","Tammuz","Av","Elul");
 	var mpy = new monthsperyeararr(12,12,13,12,12,13,12,13,12,12,13,12,12,13,12,12,13,12,13);
 
 	function weekdayarr(d0,d1,d2,d3,d4,d5,d6)
 	{
 		this[0] = d0; this[1] = d1; this[2] = d2; this[3] = d3;
 		this[4] = d4; this[5] = d5; this[6] = d6;
 	}
 
 	function gregmontharr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,m10,m11)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 	}
 
 	function hebrewmontharr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,m10,m11,m12,m13)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 		this[12] = m12; this[13] = m13;
 	}
 
 	function monthsperyeararr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,
 							  m10,m11,m12,m13,m14,m15,m16,m17,m18)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 		this[12] = m8; this[13] = m13; this[14] = m14; this[15] = m15;
 		this[16] = m16; this[17] = m17; this[18] = m18;
 	}
 	function getToday()
 	{
 		if(today == null) {
 			today = new Date();
 
 			afterSundown = (today.getHours() >= 19);
 		}
 	}
 	function displayWeekday()
 	{
 		document.writeln(gWeekday[today.getDay()] + "day");
 	}
 	function getFullYear(d)
 	{
 	    var y = d.getYear();
 
 	    if (y < 1000)
 	    	y += 1900;
 
 	    return y;
 	}
 
 	function displayGregorianDate()
 	{
 		document.writeln(gMonth[today.getMonth()] + " " + today.getDate() + ", " + getFullYear(today));
 	}
 	function displayHebrewDate()
 	{
 		if(hebrewDate != 0 && hebrewMonth != 0 && hebrewYear != 0)
 			document.writeln(hebrewDate + " " + hMonth[hebrewMonth-1] + " " + hebrewYear);
 	}
 	function GregorianToSdn(inputYear,inputMonth,inputDay)
 	{
 		var year = 0,
 			month = 0,
 			sdn;
 		// Make year a positive number
 		if (inputYear < 0)
 			year = inputYear + 4801;
 		else
 			year = inputYear + 4800;
 		// Adjust the start of the year
 		if (inputMonth > 2) {
 			month = inputMonth - 3;
 		}
 		else {
 			month = inputMonth + 9;
 			year--;
 		}
 		sdn	 = Math.floor((Math.floor(year / 100) * DAYS_PER_400_YEARS) / 4);
 		sdn += Math.floor(((year % 100) * DAYS_PER_4_YEARS) / 4);
 		sdn += Math.floor((month * DAYS_PER_5_MONTHS + 2) / 5);
 		sdn += inputDay - GREG_SDN_OFFSET;
 
 		if(afterSundown) {
 			sdn++;
 		}
 		return sdn;
 	}
 	function SdnToHebrew(sdn)
 	{
 		var inputDay,
 			tishri1 = 0,
 			tishri1After = 0,
 			yearLength = 0,
 		inputDay = sdn - HEB_SDN_OFFSET;
 		FindTishriMolad(inputDay);
 		tishri1 = Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 		if (inputDay >= tishri1) {
 			// It found Tishri 1 at the start of the year.
 			hebrewYear = metonicCycle * 19 + metonicYear + 1;
 			if (inputDay < tishri1 + 59) {
 				if (inputDay < tishri1 + 30) {
 					hebrewMonth = 1;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 1;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 2;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 - 29;
 				}
 				return;
 			}
 			// We need the length of the year to figure this out,so find Tishri 1 of the next year.
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * mpy[metonicYear];
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 			tishri1After = Tishri1((metonicYear + 1) % 19,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 		}
 		else {
 			// It found Tishri 1 at the end of the year.
 			hebrewYear = metonicCycle * 19 + metonicYear;
 			if (inputDay >= tishri1 - 177) {
 				// It is one of the last 6 months of the year.
 				if (inputDay > tishri1 - 30) {
 					hebrewMonth = 13;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 30;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 60) {
 					hebrewMonth = 12;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 60;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 89) {
 					hebrewMonth = 11;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 89;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 119) {
 					hebrewMonth = 10;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 119;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 148) {
 					hebrewMonth = 9;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 148;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 8;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 178;
 				}
 				return;
 			}
 			else {
 				if (mpy[(hebrewYear - 1) % 19] == 13) {
 					hebrewMonth = 7;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 207;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 6;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 207;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 				}
 				if (hebrewDate > 0)
 					return;
 				hebrewMonth--;
 				hebrewDate += 29;
 				if (hebrewDate > 0)
 					return;
 				// We need the length of the year to figure this out,so find Tishri 1 of this year.
 				tishri1After = tishri1;
 				FindTishriMolad(moladDay - 365);
 				tishri1 = Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 			}
 		}
 		yearLength = tishri1After - tishri1;
 		moladDay = inputDay - tishri1 - 29;
 		if (yearLength == 355 || yearLength == 385) {
 			// Heshvan has 30 days
 			if (moladDay <= 30) {
 				hebrewMonth = 2;
 				hebrewDate = moladDay;
 				return;
 			}
 			moladDay -= 30;
 		}
 		else {
 			// Heshvan has 29 days
 			if (moladDay <= 29) {
 				hebrewMonth = 2;
 				hebrewDate = moladDay;
 				return;
 			}
 			moladDay -= 29;
 		}
 		// It has to be Kislev.
 		hebrewMonth = 3;
 		hebrewDate = moladDay;
 	}
 	function FindTishriMolad(inputDay)
 	{
 		// Estimate the metonic cycle number.  Note that this may be an under
 		// estimate because there are 6939.6896 days in a metonic cycle not
 		// 6940,but it will never be an over estimate.	 The loop below will
 		// correct for any error in this estimate.
 		metonicCycle = Math.floor((inputDay + 310) / 6940);
 		// Calculate the time of the starting molad for this metonic cycle.
 		MoladOfMetonicCycle();
 		// If the above was an under estimate,increment the cycle number until
 		// the correct one is found.  For modern dates this loop is about 98.6%
 		// likely to not execute,even once,because the above estimate is
 		// really quite close.
 		while (moladDay < inputDay - 6940 + 310) {
 			metonicCycle++;
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE;
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		}
 		// Find the molad of Tishri closest to this date.
 		for (metonicYear = 0; metonicYear < 18; metonicYear++) {
 			if (moladDay > inputDay - 74)
 				break;
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * mpy[metonicYear];
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		}
 	}
 	function MoladOfMetonicCycle()
 	{
 		var r1,r2,d1,d2;
 		// Start with the time of the first molad after creation.
 		r1 = NEW_MOON_OF_CREATION;
 		// Calculate gMetonicCycle * HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE.	 The upper 32
 		// bits of the result will be in r2 and the lower 16 bits will be in r1.
 		r1 += metonicCycle * (HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE & 0xFFFF);
 		r2 = r1 >> 16;
 		r2 += metonicCycle * ((HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE >> 16) & 0xFFFF);
 		// Calculate r2r1 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY.  The remainder will be in r1,the
 		// upper 16 bits of the quotient will be in d2 and the lower 16 bits
 		// will be in d1.
 		d2 = Math.floor(r2 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 		r2 -= d2 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		r1 = (r2 << 16) | (r1 & 0xFFFF);
 		d1 = Math.floor(r1 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 		r1 -= d1 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		moladDay = (d2 << 16) | d1;
 		moladHalakim = r1;
 	}
 	function Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim)
 	{
 		var tishri1 = moladDay;
 		var dow = tishri1 % 7;
 		var leapYear =	metonicYear == 2 || metonicYear == 5 || metonicYear == 7 || metonicYear == 10 ||
 						metonicYear == 13 || metonicYear == 16 || metonicYear == 18;
 		var lastWasLeapYear =	metonicYear == 3 || metonicYear == 6 || metonicYear == 8 || metonicYear == 11 ||
 								metonicYear == 14 || metonicYear == 17 || metonicYear == 0;
 		// Apply rules 2,3 and 4
 		if ((moladHalakim >= NOON) ||
 			((!leapYear) && dow == TUES && moladHalakim >= AM3_11_20) ||
 			(lastWasLeapYear && dow == MON && moladHalakim >= AM9_32_43))
 		{
 			tishri1++;
 			dow++;
 			if (dow == 7)
 				dow = 0;
 		}
 		// Apply rule 1 after the others because it can cause an additional delay of one day.
 		if (dow == WED || dow == FRI || dow == SUN) {
 			tishri1++;
 		}
 		return tishri1;
 	}
 	//	end hiding contents from old browsers  -->
           </script>
           <script language="JavaScript" type="text/javascript">
            <!-- to hide script contents from old browsers
 
 
 	/*
 	 *	This script was adapted from C sources written by
 	 *	Scott E. Lee, which contain the following copyright notice:

 	var GREG_SDN_OFFSET = 32045,
 		DAYS_PER_5_MONTHS = 153,
 		DAYS_PER_4_YEARS = 1461,
 		DAYS_PER_400_YEARS = 146097;
 	var HALAKIM_PER_HOUR = 1080,
 		HALAKIM_PER_DAY = 25920,
 		HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE = ((29 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY) + 13753),
 		HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE = (HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * (12 * 19 + 7));
 	var HEB_SDN_OFFSET = 347997,
 		NEW_MOON_OF_CREATION = 31524,
 		NOON = (18 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR),
 		AM3_11_20 = ((9 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR) + 204),
 		AM9_32_43 = ((15 * HALAKIM_PER_HOUR) + 589);
 	var SUN = 0,
 		MON = 1,
 		TUES = 2,
 		WED = 3,
 		THUR = 4,
 		FRI = 5,
 		SAT = 6;
 	var today = null,
 		afterSundown = false,
 		hebrewMonth = 0,
 		hebrewDate = 0,
 		hebrewYear = 0,
 		metonicCycle = 0,
 		metonicYear = 0,
 		moladDay = 0,
 		moladHalakim = 0;
 	var gWeekday = new weekdayarr("Sun","Mon","Tues","Wednes","Thurs","Fri","Satur");
 	var gMonth = new gregmontharr("January","February","March","April","May","June","July","August","September","October","November","December");
 	var hMonth = new hebrewmontharr("Tishrei","Heshvan","Kislev","Tevet","Shevat","AdarI","AdarII","Nisan","Iyyar","Sivan","Tammuz","Av","Elul");
 	var mpy = new monthsperyeararr(12,12,13,12,12,13,12,13,12,12,13,12,12,13,12,12,13,12,13);
 
 	function weekdayarr(d0,d1,d2,d3,d4,d5,d6)
 	{
 		this[0] = d0; this[1] = d1; this[2] = d2; this[3] = d3;
 		this[4] = d4; this[5] = d5; this[6] = d6;
 	}
 
 	function gregmontharr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,m10,m11)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 	}
 
 	function hebrewmontharr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,m10,m11,m12,m13)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 		this[12] = m12; this[13] = m13;
 	}
 
 	function monthsperyeararr(m0,m1,m2,m3,m4,m5,m6,m7,m8,m9,
 							  m10,m11,m12,m13,m14,m15,m16,m17,m18)
 	{
 		this[0] = m0; this[1] = m1; this[2] = m2; this[3] = m3;
 		this[4] = m4; this[5] = m5; this[6] = m6; this[7] = m7;
 		this[8] = m8; this[9] = m9; this[10] = m10; this[11] = m11;
 		this[12] = m8; this[13] = m13; this[14] = m14; this[15] = m15;
 		this[16] = m16; this[17] = m17; this[18] = m18;
 	}
 	function getToday()
 	{
 		if(today == null) {
 			today = new Date();
 
 			afterSundown = (today.getHours() >= 19);
 		}
 	}
 	function displayWeekday()
 	{
 		document.writeln(gWeekday[today.getDay()] + "day");
 	}
 	function getFullYear(d)
 	{
 	    var y = d.getYear();
 
 	    if (y < 1000)
 	    	y += 1900;
 
 	    return y;
 	}
 
 	function displayGregorianDate()
 	{
 		document.writeln(gMonth[today.getMonth()] + " " + today.getDate() + ", " + getFullYear(today));
 	}
 	function displayHebrewDate()
 	{
 		if(hebrewDate != 0 && hebrewMonth != 0 && hebrewYear != 0)
 			document.writeln(hebrewDate + " " + hMonth[hebrewMonth-1] + " " + hebrewYear);
 	}
 	function GregorianToSdn(inputYear,inputMonth,inputDay)
 	{
 		var year = 0,
 			month = 0,
 			sdn;
 		// Make year a positive number
 		if (inputYear < 0)
 			year = inputYear + 4801;
 		else
 			year = inputYear + 4800;
 		// Adjust the start of the year
 		if (inputMonth > 2) {
 			month = inputMonth - 3;
 		}
 		else {
 			month = inputMonth + 9;
 			year--;
 		}
 		sdn	 = Math.floor((Math.floor(year / 100) * DAYS_PER_400_YEARS) / 4);
 		sdn += Math.floor(((year % 100) * DAYS_PER_4_YEARS) / 4);
 		sdn += Math.floor((month * DAYS_PER_5_MONTHS + 2) / 5);
 		sdn += inputDay - GREG_SDN_OFFSET;
 
 		if(afterSundown) {
 			sdn++;
 		}
 		return sdn;
 	}
 	function SdnToHebrew(sdn)
 	{
 		var inputDay,
 			tishri1 = 0,
 			tishri1After = 0,
 			yearLength = 0,
 		inputDay = sdn - HEB_SDN_OFFSET;
 		FindTishriMolad(inputDay);
 		tishri1 = Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 		if (inputDay >= tishri1) {
 			// It found Tishri 1 at the start of the year.
 			hebrewYear = metonicCycle * 19 + metonicYear + 1;
 			if (inputDay < tishri1 + 59) {
 				if (inputDay < tishri1 + 30) {
 					hebrewMonth = 1;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 1;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 2;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 - 29;
 				}
 				return;
 			}
 			// We need the length of the year to figure this out,so find Tishri 1 of the next year.
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * mpy[metonicYear];
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 			tishri1After = Tishri1((metonicYear + 1) % 19,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 		}
 		else {
 			// It found Tishri 1 at the end of the year.
 			hebrewYear = metonicCycle * 19 + metonicYear;
 			if (inputDay >= tishri1 - 177) {
 				// It is one of the last 6 months of the year.
 				if (inputDay > tishri1 - 30) {
 					hebrewMonth = 13;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 30;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 60) {
 					hebrewMonth = 12;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 60;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 89) {
 					hebrewMonth = 11;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 89;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 119) {
 					hebrewMonth = 10;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 119;
 				}
 				else if (inputDay > tishri1 - 148) {
 					hebrewMonth = 9;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 148;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 8;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 178;
 				}
 				return;
 			}
 			else {
 				if (mpy[(hebrewYear - 1) % 19] == 13) {
 					hebrewMonth = 7;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 207;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 				}
 				else {
 					hebrewMonth = 6;
 					hebrewDate = inputDay - tishri1 + 207;
 					if (hebrewDate > 0)
 						return;
 					hebrewMonth--;
 					hebrewDate += 30;
 				}
 				if (hebrewDate > 0)
 					return;
 				hebrewMonth--;
 				hebrewDate += 29;
 				if (hebrewDate > 0)
 					return;
 				// We need the length of the year to figure this out,so find Tishri 1 of this year.
 				tishri1After = tishri1;
 				FindTishriMolad(moladDay - 365);
 				tishri1 = Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim);
 			}
 		}
 		yearLength = tishri1After - tishri1;
 		moladDay = inputDay - tishri1 - 29;
 		if (yearLength == 355 || yearLength == 385) {
 			// Heshvan has 30 days
 			if (moladDay <= 30) {
 				hebrewMonth = 2;
 				hebrewDate = moladDay;
 				return;
 			}
 			moladDay -= 30;
 		}
 		else {
 			// Heshvan has 29 days
 			if (moladDay <= 29) {
 				hebrewMonth = 2;
 				hebrewDate = moladDay;
 				return;
 			}
 			moladDay -= 29;
 		}
 		// It has to be Kislev.
 		hebrewMonth = 3;
 		hebrewDate = moladDay;
 	}
 	function FindTishriMolad(inputDay)
 	{
 		// Estimate the metonic cycle number.  Note that this may be an under
 		// estimate because there are 6939.6896 days in a metonic cycle not
 		// 6940,but it will never be an over estimate.	 The loop below will
 		// correct for any error in this estimate.
 		metonicCycle = Math.floor((inputDay + 310) / 6940);
 		// Calculate the time of the starting molad for this metonic cycle.
 		MoladOfMetonicCycle();
 		// If the above was an under estimate,increment the cycle number until
 		// the correct one is found.  For modern dates this loop is about 98.6%
 		// likely to not execute,even once,because the above estimate is
 		// really quite close.
 		while (moladDay < inputDay - 6940 + 310) {
 			metonicCycle++;
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE;
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		}
 		// Find the molad of Tishri closest to this date.
 		for (metonicYear = 0; metonicYear < 18; metonicYear++) {
 			if (moladDay > inputDay - 74)
 				break;
 			moladHalakim += HALAKIM_PER_LUNAR_CYCLE * mpy[metonicYear];
 			moladDay += Math.floor(moladHalakim / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 			moladHalakim = moladHalakim % HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		}
 	}
 	function MoladOfMetonicCycle()
 	{
 		var r1,r2,d1,d2;
 		// Start with the time of the first molad after creation.
 		r1 = NEW_MOON_OF_CREATION;
 		// Calculate gMetonicCycle * HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE.	 The upper 32
 		// bits of the result will be in r2 and the lower 16 bits will be in r1.
 		r1 += metonicCycle * (HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE & 0xFFFF);
 		r2 = r1 >> 16;
 		r2 += metonicCycle * ((HALAKIM_PER_METONIC_CYCLE >> 16) & 0xFFFF);
 		// Calculate r2r1 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY.  The remainder will be in r1,the
 		// upper 16 bits of the quotient will be in d2 and the lower 16 bits
 		// will be in d1.
 		d2 = Math.floor(r2 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 		r2 -= d2 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		r1 = (r2 << 16) | (r1 & 0xFFFF);
 		d1 = Math.floor(r1 / HALAKIM_PER_DAY);
 		r1 -= d1 * HALAKIM_PER_DAY;
 		moladDay = (d2 << 16) | d1;
 		moladHalakim = r1;
 	}
 	function Tishri1(metonicYear,moladDay,moladHalakim)
 	{
 		var tishri1 = moladDay;
 		var dow = tishri1 % 7;
 		var leapYear =	metonicYear == 2 || metonicYear == 5 || metonicYear == 7 || metonicYear == 10 ||
 						metonicYear == 13 || metonicYear == 16 || metonicYear == 18;
 		var lastWasLeapYear =	metonicYear == 3 || metonicYear == 6 || metonicYear == 8 || metonicYear == 11 ||
 								metonicYear == 14 || metonicYear == 17 || metonicYear == 0;
 		// Apply rules 2,3 and 4
 		if ((moladHalakim >= NOON) ||
 			((!leapYear) && dow == TUES && moladHalakim >= AM3_11_20) ||
 			(lastWasLeapYear && dow == MON && moladHalakim >= AM9_32_43))
 		{
 			tishri1++;
 			dow++;
 			if (dow == 7)
 				dow = 0;
 		}
 		// Apply rule 1 after the others because it can cause an additional delay of one day.
 		if (dow == WED || dow == FRI || dow == SUN) {
 			tishri1++;
 		}
 		return tishri1;
 	}

                  <li>
                   <h3>
                    Summer Talmud Class with Rabbi Bolton
                   </h3>
                   <span>
                    graphics/daf_460x340.gif
                   </span>
                   <p>
                    <span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:15px;font-weight:bold;color:#000000;margin-left:0px">
                     Three Wednesdays in August | August 8, 15 &amp; 29 at 7:00 pm
                    </span>
                    <br/>
                    <span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000;margin-left:0px">
                     "The Biography of Blessings" explores the rots and the concept of blessings in the Tanakh and Rabbinic literature in order
 			 to understand how the Rabbis conceived of our system of b'rakhot.
                    </span>
                    <br/>
                    <span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
                     No previous Talmud study, nor knowledge of Hebrew or Aramaic, is required.
                    </span>
                    <br/>
                    <a href="http://www.orzarua.org/AdultEd_Talmud.shtml" style="font-family:calibri;font-size:12px;font-weight:normal;color:#0c52a4">

                  <!--
 		<li>
 			<h3>High Holy Day Study</h3>
 			<span>graphics/slideshow/mordy_460x340.gif</span>
 			<p>
 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:15px;font-weight:bold;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			Thursday, September 14, 7:00 pm - CANCELLED
 			</span>
 			<br>
 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:16px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			So Full a Voice from So Empty a Heart:<br>The Significance of the Sounds of the Shofar
 			</span>
 			<br>			
 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			There is nothing more emblematic of the High Holy Days than the shofar, yet its symbo11lic resonance may remain
             obscure. Although we find the sounds
             emitted from the shofar familiar, many of
             us remain in the dark as to the specific
             significance each sound conveys.
             <br>
             Please join Rabbi Mordecai Schwartz as he investigates
             each of the shofar sounds to
             uncover their corresponding meanings.
             The blowing of the shofar can be most
             inspiring and motivational if we
             appreciate its varied purposes as reflected
             in classical Jewish sources.
 			</span>
 			<br>
 			<a href="http://www.orzarua.org/calendar.shtml" style="font-family:calibri;font-size:12px;font-weight:normal;color:#0000cd">
 			Complete list of events</a>
 			</p>

 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;color:#313131;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">

                  <!--
 		<li>
 			<h3>Audio:  Annual Tshuvah Lecture - Rabbi Dr. Dov Weiss</h3>
 			<span>graphics/slideshow/dovWeiss_460x340.gif</span>
 			<p>
 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:15px;font-weight:bold;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			<a href="http://www.orzarua.org/audio/DovWeiss_170924.mp3" style="font-family:calibri;font-size:15px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4">
 			Listen to</a> the Sunday, September 24, 2017, Event
 			</span>
 			<br>
 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:17px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			Rabbinic Irreverence:  Imagining a Repentant God
 			</span>
 			<br>			
 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			Judaism is often described as a religion that tolerates, even celebrates, arguing with God. Unlike Christianity and Islam, 
 		it is said, Judaism endorses a tradition of protest as first expressed in the biblical stories of Abraham, Job, and Jeremiah. 
 		Less well known, however, are those Jewish texts that imagine God conceding error. Strikingly, in several of them, God even 
 		admits transgressing Torah law. In this lecture, Rabbi Weiss examined these Midrashim, and asked: Why would some Rabbis envision 
 		God as performing Tshuvah? Is God not perfect? What religious value or insight might be expressed in these radical texts?
 		As we enter Yom Kippur, how could these images reinvigorate our own Tshuvah?
 			</span>
 			<br>
 			<a href="http://www.orzarua.org/calendar.shtml" style="font-family:calibri;font-size:12px;font-weight:normal;color:#0000cd">
 			Complete list of events</a>
 			</p>
 		</li>
 		-->

 			<h3>Lucy S. Dawidowicz Lecture</h3>
 			<span>graphics/slideshow/carlebach_460x340.gif</span>
 			<p>
 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:15px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4;margin-left:0px">
 			Elisheva Carlebach, PhD

 			</span>
 			<br>
 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			Revealed Beauty and Hidden Danger:  On Jewish Books of Time in Early Modern Europe
 			</span>
 			<br>
 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			Elisheva Carlebach is the Salo Baron Professor of Jewish History, Culture, and Society, at Columbia University, specializing
 			in the cultural, intellectual, and religious history of the Jews in Early Modern Europe.
 			<br>
 			Through an animated talk and visual exhibit Dr. Carlebach, the Salo Baron Professor of Jewish History, Culture, and Society, at Columbia University, will 	
 			illuminate the surprising significance and sumbolism of Jewish calendars within the majority Christian societies from which they emerged.
 			<br>
 The annual Lucy S. Dawidowicz lecture honors the memory of a great historian of the Holocaust and member of Or Zarua. The lectures mark the birthday of the Congregation. After the lecture, dessert and birthday cake will be served in honor of OZ's 29th birthday.
             <br>
 			There is no charge to attend, but RSVP for security and planning purposes to dwenger@orzarua.org or x39

 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			The Book of Jonah is chanted on Yom Kippur afternoon as the haftarah at
 minhah. The basic story may be well known - a reluctant prophet, a storm at sea,
 3 days in a whale, but important details about Jonah's refusal to be a prophet,
 the sea voyage and his companions reactions, and his time in the belly of a big
 fish (not a whale!) help us learn the lessons that stand at the center of this great
 work. Among the themes we will explore are: Jonah's
 relationship, and thus Jews' relationships, to the nations of the
 world; Jonah's prayer life and the possibilities of prayer; linguistic
 connections between Jonah and other important stories in the
 Bible.
 			</span>
 			<br>
 			<a href="http://www.orzarua.org/calendar.shtml" style="font-family:calibri;font-size:12px;font-weight:normal;color:#0000cd">
 			Complete list of events</a>
 			</p>
 		</li-->

 	Shabbat Shirah - Tu BiSh'vat - O"Z 24th Birthday Celebrations
 	</span>
 	<table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 	This year, our Or Zarua birthday celebration falls out on Shabbat Shirah (the Sabbath whose parashah contains the crossing of the sea and the song of celebration sung by the Israelites after crossing) and on Tu BiSh'vat (The New Year of Trees). We have some wonderful plans to celebrate so please join us!
 <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 Friday night, January 25th, come to Friday night services, which will be followed at 6:00 pm by refreshments and a special Shabbat Zimriyah - a sing-a-long to emphasize the special musical character of Shabbat Shirah. Rabbis Amy & Scott Bolton will teach a few new tunes, and we'll sing lots of familiar ones as well.
 <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 At Shabbat morning services we'll have some reflections about music and our prayer experience with Marc Ashley and Dr. Terry Krulwich, and Marc Ashley will teach some tunes that we'll use during Musaf.  For a taste, listen to <a href="http://www.orzarua.org/audio/ShabbatShirah_5773.mp3">this</a>...
 <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 Then, after services, we'll have our annual birthday Kiddush and lunch, which is open to all. Come celebrate with us, sing, enjoy Tu B'Shvat and make it an O"Z birthday to remember!

               <span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:17px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4;margin-left:0px">
                Daily Minyan
               </span>
               <table>
                <tr>
                 <td height="1px">
                 </td>
                </tr>
               </table>
               <img src="http://www.orzarua.org/graphics/minyan3_300x176.gif"/>
               <table>
                <tr>
                 <td height="1px">
                 </td>
                </tr>
               </table>
               <div style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px; line-height:1.10em">
                Join us for daily minyan Mon-Fri 7:15am, Sundays 8:45am, Rosh Hodesh 7am.
                <table>
                 <tr>
                  <td height="1px">
                  </td>
                 </tr>
                </table>
                There is power, joy and a great sense of calm in starting the day with daily prayers. Our sanctuary provides inspiration, and it's uplifting to make the strong move to be part of the minyan. Those who are saying kaddish rely on our community. Join us for wonderful breakfast and conversation afterwards or get to your next event of the day better prepared! Our tradition teaches that one of the pillars of the world is prayer, so please add yours at Or Zarua.
               </div>
               <table>
                <tr>
                 <td height="18px">
                 </td>
                </tr>

               <span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:16px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4;margin-left:0px">
                Make Kabbalat Shabbat a Priority!
               </span>
               <table>
                <tr>
                 <td height="1px">
                 </td>
                </tr>
               </table>
               <div style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px; line-height:1.10em">
                Enjoy the transition from
                <b>
                 chol
                </b>
                (the weekday) to the
                <b>
                 kedushah
                </b>
                (holiness) of Shabbat
 	during Minhah and Kabbalat Shabbat/Ma'ariv services.  It can be truly transformative - but only
 	if you're here to experience it!
                <table>
                 <tr>
                  <td height="1px">
                  </td>
                 </tr>
                </table>
                Make the commitment to attend by
                <a href="http://goo.gl/forms/ZUobbhvjjq" style="font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;color:#0000ad;font-weight:bold">
                 signing up
                </a>
                , even
 	if just for one time.  The current week's service time is listed at the far right side of each
 	page of our website.
               </div>
               <table>
                <tr>
                 <td height="18px">
                 </td>
                </tr>

 <Span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:16px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4">
 Surprise: The Poetics of the Unexpected from Milton to Austen
 </Span>
 <table><tr><td height="4px"></td></tr></table>
 <Span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">
 Saturday, May 16, after Kiddush
 </Span>
 <br>
 <Span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000">	
 Congregant Christopher Miller, associate professor of English at the College of Staten Island
 (CUNY), specializes in the poetry and prose fiction of the Long Eighteenth Century - that is, from the late seventeenth century
 through the Romantic era. After kiddush on Saturday, May 16, he will be discussing his recently published book <i>Surprise: The Poetics of the
 Unexpected from Milton to Austen</i>. The book studies the changes in the meaning of surprise in fiction "from violent attack
 to pleasurable experience, and from external event to internal feeling."

 <div style="margin-left:0px;font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000">
 Throughout history poetry has made people reflect in unique ways on key aspects of their lives. Rabbi Scott Bolton and Congregant Nir Yarden will host a new poetry club at Or Zzrua dedicated to reading and discussing important works of poetry that have a common theme on important aspects of our lives. The theme for our first poetry reading and discussion will be loss and coping. What do the great poets and poems throughout history teach us about losses in our lives and how we cope with those losses, be it loss of life, loved ones or faith? We will look at selections ranging from Tanakh to Emily Dickinson and Yehuda Amichai. Join us for a stimulating evening of readings and discussion. Or just come to listen and be inspired. All poems to be read will be distributed at the meeting. 
 <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 For questions and to RSVP, contact <a href="mailto:nyarden@yardenlawfirm.com">Nir</a>. Weather permitting, we'll be under the stars on the roof.
 </div>

 Lucy Dawidowicz Memorial Lecture

 <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 <span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:bold;text-align:justify;color:#000000;margin-left:0px">
 Thursday, February 4, 2016 at 7:30 pm

 <div style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000">
 Jeremy Dauber, professor of Yiddish in the Department of Germanic Languages at Columbia University:&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>Stop Me If You've Heard This One Before: Some New Thoughts on Jewish Comedy</b>. 
 <table><tr><td height="1px"></td></tr></table>
 Professor Dauber grew up in Teaneck, NJ, and spent a year in Israel before attending Harvard. He received his doctorate, in Modern Jewish Studies, from Oxford University. He is the author of several books and of numerous articles, essays and reviews. His research interests include Yiddish literature of the early modern period, Hebrew and Yiddish literature of the 19th century, the Yiddish theater, and American Jewish literature and popular culture.

 Hevruta: Or Zarua Talmud Seminar
 </span>
 
 <table><tr><td height="8px"></td></tr></table>
 	
 
 <div style="width:334px;font-family:calibri;font-size:16px;font-weight:normal;text-align:justify;color:#000000;">
 
     			<span class="dkgr16bC">
                 <b>Learn to Study Talmud On Your Own</b>
 				</span>
 				<table><tr><td height="4px"></td></tr></table>
 				
 				
 						<div style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;text-align:justify;color:#000000;margin-left:0px">
         The Talmud is central to Judaism yet relatively few really know what it is, due in large part to its difficult style and structure.  This course is designed to
 		teach us how  to crack the code of the Talmud. Get the insider's view of Talmudic philosophy, logic, perspective on Jewish history and development of the law.
 		Whether your Hebrew background is deep or just at the phonetic readers' level, you can develop the vocabulary and conceptual approaches needed to unlock the
 		Talmud's language and structure.

 <table><tr><td height="18px"></td></tr></table>
 <TABLE style="padding:4px;width:340px;border:solid 0px #0c52a4;background-color:#ffffff">
 	<tr>
 		<td>
 <span  style="font-family:calibri;font-size:18px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4">
 Jews & Jazz
 </span>
 <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 			<span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:15px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4;margin-left:0px">
 			Loren Schoenberg</i>
 			</span>
 			<table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 			<div style="font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:bold;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			Sunday, January 10, 2016, at 7:00 pm
 			</div>
 
 <div style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 Jazz is a genre of music
 that originated in
 African-American communities
 in the late
 19th and early 20th
 centuries. The extensive
 list of African-Americans
 who have contributed to
 the development of jazz includes Scott
 Joplin, Louis Armstrong, Duke Ellington,
 and Charlie Parker. However, a wide variety
 of people from other ethnic groups have
 also influenced the development of jazz.
 Among them are Jewish composers and
 musicians including Harold Arlen, Irving
 Berlin, George Gershwin, Benny Goodman,
 Jerome Kern, and Artie Shaw.
 <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 Loren Schoenberg, Founding Director
 and Senior Scholar of The National Jazz
 Museum in Harlem, will be discussing the
 Jewish role in the history of jazz on
 Sunday, January 10, at 7:00 p.m. "Jews
 and Jazz" is free of charge and open to all.
 <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 			
 			<a href="http://www.orzarua.org/scholars.shtml" style="font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:normal;color:#0c52a4">
 			More information about this series</a>
 			</span>
 		</td>
 	</tr>
 </TABLE>

 <table><tr><td height="18px"></td></tr></table>
 <TABLE style="padding:4px;width:340px;border:solid 0px #0c52a4;background-color:#ffffff">
 	<tr>
 		<td>
 <span  style="font-family:calibri;font-size:18px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4">
 Shabbat Shirah Shabbaton
 </span>
 <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 <DIV style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000">
 	<Span style="font-weight:bold">
     Friday and Saturday, January 22 and 23, 2016
     </span>
     <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
     <Span style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4">
     Dr. Marsha Bryan Edelman and Friends of Zamir
     </span>
     <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 	Dr. Edelman is an adjunct professor of music and education at Gratz College and conductor of HaZamir Philadelphia, a chapter of the Jewish Choral Foundation. Friends of Zamir Ensemble, directed by Dr. Edelman, will be joining Or Zarua for Shabbat Shirah, when we read Parshat Beshalah which includes Shirat HaYam. The Shabbaton will begin with Kabbalat Shabbat and Shabbat dinner (RSVP/fee) and will include an illuminated performance after Kiddush at 1 p.m.

 <table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>

 			Visiting Scholars Teach Torah</i>

 			<table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 			<div style="font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:bold;color:#000000;text-align:justify; margin-left: 0px">
 			
       			
       			September 30, 2015 - Rabbi Robert Harris
           			<div style="margin-left:10px;font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:normal;color:#0c52a4;">
       				<b>A Sukkot Like None Ever Celebrated Before:  Ezra, the Torah Book, and the Return from Exile</b>
           				<div style="margin-left:10px;color:#000000;font-size:14px">
       					During the 5th century BCE, amidst a second wave of Jewish return from Babylonian exile, Ezra the Scribe (a magistrate of 
       					the Persian Empire) read from the Torah to the assembled Judean community in Jerusalem.  He did so under the watchful 
       					tutelage of Nehemiah, the Persian Governor and fellow Judean.  Reading about the festival calendar in what we now call 
       					Leviticus 23, they made a startling discovery.  We will explore this discovery - and how the Judeans reacted - and will 
       					discuss its implications for Judaism, down to our present day.
       					<table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
       					Following "Bring Your Own" Dinner in the Sukkah
       					<table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
       						Rabbi Harris is an Associate professor of Bible at The Jewish Theological Seminary&nbsp;&nbsp;
       						<a href="http://www.jtsa.edu/Academics/Faculty_Profiles/Robert_Harris_Bio.xml?ID_NUM=100232"

       			<table><tr><td height="8px"></td></tr></table>
       			
 			October 24, 2015 - Dr. David G. Roskies
 				<div style="margin-left:10px;font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:normal;color:#0c52a4;">
 				<b>Jewspeak:  How We Became the People of the Spoken Word</b>
 					<div style="margin-left:10px;color:#000000;font-size:14px">
 					First, the Jews created a Jewish vernacular called Yiddish. Then they produced a few playwrights, prose writers and 
 					poets who figured out how to represent the way Jews - male and female, old and young, rich and poor, alive and dead - spoke, 
 					cursed, joked, played, sang and cried. Then the greatest of these writers, Sholem Aleichem, took this written-as-spoken language 
 					on the road. Reaching North America, he discovered how much the Yiddish language could absorb from English before it became thoroughly un-Jewed.
 					<table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 						Dr. Roskies is the Sol and Evelyn Henkind Chair in Yiddish Literature and Culture and professor of Jewish Literature of The Jewish 
 						Theological Seminary&nbsp;&nbsp;<a href="http://www.jtsa.edu/Academics/Faculty_Profiles/David_Roskies_Bio.xml?ID_NUM=100490" 	
 						style="font-family:calibri;font-size:12px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4;">Dr. Roskies' bio</a>
     				</div>
                 </div>
 			
 			<table><tr><td height="8px"></td></tr></table>
 			May 21, 2016 - Dr. Alan Mintz
 				<div style="margin-left:10px;font-family:calibri;font-size:13px;font-weight:normal;color:#0c52a4;">
 				<b>It's Not About Eternity:  Rosh Hodesh and the Shape of Jewish Time</b>
 					 <div style="margin-left:10px;color:#000000;font-size:14px">
 					 We will explore the profound way in which Judaism shapes our lives by regulating the rhythms 
 					  time.  The biblical invention of the pattern of 6 +1 had an enormous impact on all Western religions.  Yet we now live within a 
 					  culture in which time has been flattened.  What do Judaism's insights about time teach about how to live our lives? 
 					<table><tr><td height="2px"></td></tr></table>
 						Dr. Mintz is the Chana Kekst Professor of Hebrew Literature in the Department of Jewish Literature of the The Jewish Theological Seminary
 						&nbsp;&nbsp;<a href="http://www.jtsa.edu/Academics/Faculty_Profiles/Alan_Mintz_Bio.xml?ID_NUM=12629" 	
 						style="font-family:calibri;font-size:12px;font-weight:bold;color:#0c52a4;">Dr. Mintz' bio</a>
     				 </div>

 <table><tr><td height="12px"></td></tr></table>
 <table style="padding:2px;width:715px;border:solid 7px #e9e9e9;background-color:#ffffff">
 <tr>
 <td>
 <div style="font-family:calibri;font-size:16px;font-weight:normal;color:#0c52a4;">
 <b>Shabbat Morning Youth Programs</b>
 </div>
 <table><tr><td height="1px"></td></tr></table>
 <div style="font-family:calibri;font-size:14px;font-weight:normal;color:#000000;margin-left:10px">
 Our Shabbat prayer and learning experiences for children and teens are fun and inspiring!  We provide age appropriate services and activities from early childhood through high school.  All programs begin at 10:30 a.m. and conclude with a light kiddush and snack.
 <table><tr><td height="1px"></td></tr></table>
 <b>Kef Shabbat:</b>  Starting with our youngest children (infant to pre-K), we meet every Saturday in the large classroom on the 7th floor. Parents and children join together to celebrate Shabbat in song, prayer, movement and interactive learning experiences. Through Kef Shabbat, designed by Rabbi Amy Bolton in collaboration with a dedicated group of parent volunteers, children learn the basics of the Shabbat service with singing and dancing, participate in a creative weekly Torah portion or holiday activity, enjoy Kiddush with blessings and listen to a story related to the Torah portion or holiday. Parents accompany their children, participate in the service and activities, and enjoy the social camaraderie with other parents of young children.
 <table><tr><td height="1px"></td></tr></table>
 <b>Ruach Shabbat</b>, first through third grade, is led by Eliana Light.  The service, also on the 7th floor, is filled with fun, music, and lots of spirit. The focus is both on the "what" of t'fillah, through skill building and singing, as well as the "why" and the "how" of t'fillah, through fun games and activities.  The children learn about the parsha (weekly Torah portion), holidays and Jewish values and perform a "Mitzvah Mission" each week.  Parents are welcome to participate.
 <table><tr><td height="1px"></td></tr></table> 
 <b>Mah Zeh Shabbat</b>, which means, "Whoa, this is SOME fantastic Shabbat minyan!" is designed for our 4th grade through middle school group and meets in the library in the 4th floor.   Led by Sigal Hirsch and Elana Mendelowitz, the service is filled with spirited davening, singing and discussion.  The children begin to take on greater leadership roles in the service.
 <table><tr><td height="1px"></td></tr></table>
 <b>Teen Group</b> (7th through high school) meets for a special service and Kiddush once per month in the library.  Originally launched by congregant Laurie Dien and led by Sigal and Elana, the service is hands on with tweens and teens leading and enjoying a Kiddush lunch afterwards.  This is a great opportunity for your post Bar mitzvah student to meet and socialize with other Jewish tweens and teens.
 </div>
 <table><tr><td height="1px"></td></tr></table>
 </div>
 </td>
 </tr>
